Carter phone calls cost CBS $5o,ooo 
BEDMINSTER. N J. (A P) - CBS* telephone bill for Saturday’s nationally broadcast two-hour radio phone-in pro­ gram featuring President Carter was 
$5o.(NH), roughly $1,19(1 for each of the 
42 calls that got through, officials said 
Monday. 
A spokesman for AT&T Long Lines 
Division said the $5(1.(HK) paid for set­ ting up the special HOU arca code that kept the estimated nine million unsuc­ cessful callers from jamming normal phone serv ice. 
Also figured into the bill were the costs of management, use of phone lines and installation of phones in the 
White House. 

Teachers endorse 
3 non-incumbents 

A political slap in the face was dealt to the South San Antonio 
School D istrict tru stees Mon­ day. 
Teachers in that district endorsed three candidates fur the April 2 school 
In la rd election, hut none of them were incumbents. 
Teachers say the current board's refusal to work with them forced them to got involved in the race. 
“ We have been trying all year to reason with the board, and they 

 haven't cooperated,’’ Haul Prado, pre­ sident of the South San Antonio 
Teachers’ Assn. said Monday. 
“ They left us no alternative but to try to seek trustees who would favor working with the teachers' organiza­ tion.” 

This is the first time South San An­ tonio Teachers* Assn.’s political arm has entered school board politics. 
Candidates endorsed by the teachers 
Monday are Pete Hernandez, Nick 
Monreal and John Saldana. 

Saldana is a former school board member. Monreal ran for the office last year. He is also a frequent oppon­ ent of the board at meetings. 
Eight candidates are in this year’s race, including incumbent Eugene 
Johnson and John Leal. 

Leal was appointed less than a month ago to take the place of John 
Mac hado, who resigned. 
Eugene Rodriguez, who currently sits on the board, did not file for re­ election.

A former San Antonio man serving time in a federal prison iii Indiana 
Monday asked to have his rap sheet cleared ut live old arrests lodged against him here. 
The charges — dating hack to 1967, 
1971 and 1974 but still on his arrest record or rap sheet — were subse­ quently dismissed, according to the net it ion filed by Edward Maldonado 
Benavides in Blist District Court here. 
Benavides is currently serving a 

15-year sentence in Terre Haute, Iud.. in the federal penitentiary there 
His petition, filed under a pauper s oath by mail. asks the court specifi­ cally to order San Antonio Polic e Chief 
F E Peters to erase the five arrests from his record. 

Benavides, on his own behalf, claims those arrests color his prospects for parole, work or study release or other benefits negative^.

Southwest Texas State in his playing days and led SWT to the NAIA cham ­ pionship in I HHD after a third place finish a year earlier.

Black colleges losing the stars 

A decade or so ago, som e of the m ost talen ted c o lle g ia te p la y ers in the country w ere never heard of sim ply because they played for sm a ll black colleges. 

Major universities such as Texas, 
AAM. Arkansas, Tennessee, Alabama and Ole Miss refused to recruit the black athlete. Thus, schools such as 
Grambling. Texas Southern. Prairie 
View, Alcorn AAM and Jackson State w ere loaded vs it Ii som e of the best young talent in sports. 
Slowly but surely, it began changing. 
A speedy gridder from Beaumont He­ bert by the name of Jerry Le Vias got it started in the SWC by attending SMU. ta te r, such names as Bubba Bean, 
Roosevelt Leaks, Stable Vincent, Ike 
F o rte , R odrigo B arn es and A ndre 
Tillman earned spots on SWC rosters. 

It has progressed to the point where it Is not uncommon for such names as tam Jones or Curtis Dickey and Ben 
Cowens to be signed by SWC schools. 

It is obvious that black athletes have strengthened the m ajor colleges but what is not so obvious is how the small black schools have suffered. 
Not only iii football but all sports. 
Take the current college basketball season. When A rk a n sas, the SWC champion, lines up for the tipoff in 
NCAA playoff action, five blacks will be starting for the Hogs. 
Tile key to the recent success of 
Alabama and Tennessee’s basketball programs are the black players, 
Years ago the small black colleges cornified only against each other for the top black athletes. Now they must recruit against all schools, including the b ig gest u n iv e rsitie s in the 
■ country. 
It has not been easy for the tiny black schools. It is gelling harder and harder to recruit successfully. * 

Talent divided. 

Take North Carolina Central, for in­ stance. Once a cage powerhouse. NCC was 3-24 this year. 
Look at Delaware Stale, once blessed with some et the best black players in the nation This year, Coach Marshall 
Em ery’• Delaware St. team won two and lost 25. 
“ The major Southern white schools have drained the local talent to the 
I mint where it's very difficult to go to the South and attract even a second- line player,” says Em ery, 
Back when the major schools would not recruit blacks, the sm all black colleges could recruit all the talent they needed within a 2oo-milt* radius of the school. 

Morton, Ramsey swap teams, fans 

C om petition from the m a jo r universities has changed that, though. 
Even the small black schools now must rely heavily on out-of-state recruiting from basketball hotbeds. 
North Carolina Central, as an exam ­ ple, signed five freshm en recently. 
Four of those youngsters cam e from small high schools in Washington. 

In other words, the black talent is now being divided by the whole country , not just by black schools. 

The Mid-E astern A thletic C onfer­ ence (MEAC) is typical of the black college leag ue today. 
The season-ending cage tourney once aver­ aged Kl.(Kilt per night. The MEAC tourney which recently ended barely- averaged 3.IMIo per session. 
One coach says that a student apolo­ gized for not a ttend ing the to u rn a ­ ment. “ He said he had to go som e­ where else to see the real good teams play,” says the coach. 
Against outside competition, MEAC team s won only 29 per cent of their games this season. 
The talent is so divided that small black schools simply do not have the resources to I m - national powers today. 

Hard to fight 

The sm all black schools are now no 

 different than the sm all white schools 

 iii that they have learned it is impos­ sible lo consistently fight and defeat big business. 
T rinity c a n 't rec ru it with Texas. 
Howard Payne can't recruit with A&M. 
Texas L utheran c a n 't recru it with 
Texas Tech. And Delaware State can't recruit with Michigan or Ohio State or 
Penn State or Colorado, etc. 
E m ery explains the real problem when he sa y s. “ I offer a boy a cheeseburger and Dean Smith (North 
Carolina) offers him a steak dinner.” 

I f s a sim ple case of the m a jo r schools having more to offer. 

But Emery says there is more to it than that. “ On top of that the parents of black players are still into that old 
*if-it’s*w h ite-it-m u st-b e-b etter' ay n- d r Ollie. They still think the w hite man s ice is colder than ours.’’ 
Emery says one advantage the black schools still have is that they have black coaches “ Let's face it.” he say s, 
“ many white coaches think their black players can't be disciplined. They re afraid.” 

But as major schools continue to hire more black coaches, the black schools will lose this so-called adv antage. 
Before we know it, you won t be able to tell a sm all black school from a small white school And what’s wrong with that?

Burbank prepares for SOC, 

SP O R TS 

Tuesday March 8 1977 

H 
SAN ANTONIO EXPRESS— Tuesdoy March 8 1977 
Burbank meets 
SOC in tourney 

By JOHN HINES 
Or THE EXPRESS STAPE 

Burbank will play Dallas South Oak 
Cliff (33-8) in the semifinals of the state basketball tournament at 8 p.m. 
Friday at the University of Texas' 
Gregory Gym. 
The opening Class AAAA semifinal matches Fort Worth Dunbar (38-1) and 
Houston Westchester (32-9) at 4 p.m. 
Friday. 
The finals are set for 2:o5 p.m. 
Saturday. 
Class B will hold its entire tourney 
Saturday. In the semis, it's Leggett 
(36-4) vs. Avinger (34-7) at 8:3o a m., then Krum (38-5) vs. Hedley (35-4) at 
IO a.m. Finals tip off is at 8 p.m. 
Burbank will be trying for double revenge on Oak Cliff, for the Dallas school has beaten the last two Alamo 
City teams it has faced in the state tourney, the Jefferson boys (1o9-1oo in 
1974) and Clemens girls (79-65) two weeks ago. 
Preparation 

The Bulldogs Monday began prepar­ ations for South Oak Cliff, based on information from Coaches Hon Lloyd of Wheatley and Roland Lopez of Fox 
Tech, who scouted the College Station regional. 
Oak Cliff's starters are B-4 Kicky 
Phillips, 6-3 Arthur Williams, 6-2 Mark 
Coleman, 6-2 David Burns and 5-7 Cul­ len Mayfield. Coleman and Mayfield are the guards. 
Mayfield is a very quick type of guard, uses both hands well and has good range from 15-2o feet. 
Bums and Williams are good from the 2o-25 foot range, with Burns a 
“ streak shooter.” They typify the Gol­ den Bear offense, which will put the 

 ball up from anywhere. 
They don’t go inside much, but when they do, Phillips is a very effective rebounder. 
Zone defense 
South Oak Cliff sets up in a 2-3 zone defense. 
An idea of Oak C liff’s potentcy comes from the fact that they are the only team to beat Dunbar (8o-78 in overtime). 
Dunbar’s starters are 6-9 James 
Griffin, 6-3 Thomas Glenn, 5-9 point guard Jeffrey Kirven and regular guards Michael Watley, 6-3, and Cletis 
Hubbard, 6-o. 
“ These people are not like most 
Houston or Dallas teams, they will control the ball, too, and go to a four- corner,” says Highlands Coach John 
Kemmerzehl, who scouted the Abilene regional along with Sam Houston’s Pat 
Caza. 
“ Griffin is their big stud, he hooks with both hands. Glenn jumps like 
Charles Bean of Houston, while Kirven is in the category of being a step quicker than Freddy Medina (La­ mer).’’ 
'76 champs out 
Dunbar beat defending state cham­ pion El Paso Eastwood, 68-63, in the regional finals, in a good matchup 
(Eastwood’s starters were 6-8, 6-8, 6-5, 
6-4 and 5-11). 
“ Eastwood missed a couple of easy shots and Dunbar got the ball and scored and that was the difference.,” 
Kemmerzehl concluded. “ They are extremely quick in bringing the bill down.” 
Westchester defeated four-time state champ Houston Wheatley in its re­ gional finals, 74-71.

POMPANO BEACH , 
Fla. (AP) — Kookie in­ fielder Bump Wills gave ground in contract nego­ tiations Monday and signed a one-year con­ tract with the Texas 
Hangers, general manager Dan O’Brien said. 
Wills had been report­ ed to be holding out for a three-year contract at 
$4(1.(MM) a year. 
O’Brien did not specify what Wills’ salary will be, but indicated it would not be accurate to specu­ late he w as making more than the minimum salary of $19.(HIO 
“ All parties were happy with the final agreement.” O’Brien said. “ Hopefully, he’ll go out now with a second- base job.” 
W ills was the last player to be signed to the 
Hanger's 45-man train­ ing platoon here.

Phoenix, Knicks keep drifting out of1977 NBA playoff picture 

ASSOCUTtD PRISS lf (he* National Basketball Assoria-' 
(ion playoffs were to begin today, among those watching on television would be tile Phoenix Suns, last year's losing finalists, and the New York 
Knicks, with their $2.5 million payroll. 
What’s more. neither team seems likely to change from spectator to participant in the remaining five weeks of the regular season. 
The defending champion Boston 
Celtics and the revamped Kansas City 
Kings have taken commanding posi­ tions in the races for the two final playoff berths, which would lock out the Suns and Knicks, among others. 
Under the playoff format adopted this season, 12 of the 22 NBA teams qualify for post-season play—the four division winners, plus the four teams with the next best records in each conference. 

The division winners receive byes through the first round. The other four clubs in each conference are listed in order of their winning percentages. with No. I playing No. 4 and No. 2 meeting No. 3 iii best-of-three series to reduce the number of playoff teams to eight. 
After that, each series is best-of-se- ven, with the team with the better record getting the home-court advan­ tage for the odd game, 
If the playoffs were to start today, instead of the second week in April, the qualifiers would be: 
Eastern Conference: Washington, 

Philadelphia. Houston, San Antonio. 
Cleveland and Boston. 
Western Conference: Denver, Los 
Angeles, Portland, Detroit, Golden 
State and Kansas City. 
A testament to the fairness of this playoff system is that there are 12 teams in the NBA with winning records, and all 12 would make the playoffs. 
The New York Knicks are about the only other team in the running for a playoff spot in the East, and their chances do not look good. Sunday’s 
116-1o2 triumph at Philadelphia raised their record to 29-35 but left them four games behind Boston and 5*2 back of 
Cleveland. 
“ We have all the ingredients for a good team,” says Knicks Coach Hod 
Holzman, who announced Saturday that he will slop down at the end of the season, “ but they haven’t blended together. The chemistry is not there yet,” 

Despite the acquisition of three-time scoring champion Bob McAdoo, the 
Knicks appear headed for their third straight losing season and their second out of the playoffs. 
And Boston has been playing well of late, witness Sunday’s 112-11oovertime win over powerful Denver. Center 
Dave Cowens is rounding into top shape after his leave of absence, and guard Charlie Scott is almost ready to return after being sidelined with a broken hand. 
Iii the.West, Kansas City— with 

 ex-ABAers' Hon Boone and Brian Tay­ lor and rookie Richard Washington playing prominent roles—has a 
2*2-game lead over Seattle in their battle for the last playoff spot. What’s more, the Sonics have just begun a nine-game road trip, losing the opener 

 of their odyssey 
Saturday. 
134-1o4 at Portland 

A dark horse here is Chicago, which- has recovered from a miserable start to win its last seven and now trails the 
Kings by .just three games.

By CLIFFORD BRO YLES 
Of THI EXPRESS ST Aff 

SEQ U IN — The Texas Lutheran 
College Bulldogs must learn to face life without Steve Porter. 
When the Bulldogs open their 1977-78 season next November, Porter will be absent after a scintillating four-year career. 
The 6-8 Porter closed out his re­ cord-breaking stay (He is the school’s all-time leading scorer and rebounder) against East Texas State when the 
Bulldogs bowed in the opening round of the NAIA playoffs. 
Where to now? Porter has carried the Bulldogs a long way the past four years. Now TLF must find a new mode of transportation. 
Super year 

“ Steve had an exceptional year for us." said TLC Coach Jim Shuler Mon­ day, “ and against East Texas we just didn’t have anybody to go in and take over for him except for Anderson 
(Rodney, 6-5, who had 18 points off the bench). ♦ 
“ We may have relied a little too much on Steve and we may have to do things a little differently next year without out him.” 
TLC was 21-1o this season, the first 
2o-win campaign at the school since the pre-World War ll days of 1938. and 
73-35 in Porter’s four seasons. 
Shuler is determined to find some­ body to replace Porter, although doing it will be easier said than dune. 
Big returnee 
Hon Glover, 6-8 freshman, is the only thing resembling a big man on the 
TLT roster and he is known for his outside shooting. 
# 
“ We’ve got to have somebody that can post down low for us,” said Shuler. 
“ I ve been working with Hon and he is just not used to playing inside. You’ve got to work so hard to get open. For every five times you work open, you only get the ball once." 
With 12 returning squadmen, scho­ larships will not be too abundant at 
TLF this season, but Shuler is hoping to fill one of his openings with a nota­ ble big man. 
Dennis Tealer, the 6-5 junior from 
Gonzales, could be a factor next sea­ son, but his availability is questionable because of a knee injury. 
“ lie s just got lo come back better for lls.” agreed Shuler 
Bit things have been expected from 
Tealer, hut as yet he has only produced in spurts. 
His season ended prematurely when lie had a freak injury to Ins left knee before the East Texas game. It has been diagnosed as a sprain and will not require surgery (although Shuler plans to seek another medical opin­ ion). 
Besides Porter, only seniors Conrad 
Sture and Don Schmitt will be missing 

 next season. 
TLC has five guards returning, in­ cluding starters Dvvain Thomas and 
Mike Jones. Also back will be James 
Goodman, David Kahle and Will Pier­ son. 
Inside returnees include Anderson, 
Glover, Alfred Silva. Mike Harris, 
Tealer and Ken Hamilton. 
Anderson, who came off the bench to hit nine of ll from the field against 
East Texas, could be a key factor. 
“ Every year I seem to make a mistake oil somebody and Rodney was my mistake this'year," said Shuler. 
“ He should have been playing a lot more than he did.” 
R ockets fly by Buffalo 

BUFFALO (AP) — Seven-foot Kevin 
Kunnert. averaging only 8.6 points a game, poured in a career-high 31 points and pulled down 13 rebounds 
Monday night as the streaking Houston 
Rockets rolled to a 128*1o7 National 
Basketball Association victory over the 
Buffalo Braves. 
The triumph left the second-place 
Rockets just 1*2 games behind Wa­ shington i i i the Central Division. 
Houston fell behind 37-26 after the opening period hut surged to a 64*54 halftime bulge by outscoring Buffalo 
38-17 in the second quarter as Rudy 
Tomjanovich hit for 12 points, John 
Lucas IO and Kunnert eight. 
Houston nailed down its fourth consecutive victory by connecting on 6o of 1o3 shots from the field for 58 per cent. 
Lucas made two layups—one off a steal, the other on a drive—and Tom­ janovich banked in a long shot as the 
Rockets moved from a 48-48 tie to a six-point lead and were never headed. 
They broke it open with a 1o-point run—baskets by Lucas and Kunnert, two by Malone, plus two free throws by 
Kunnert—for un 8o-6o spread in the third period. 
Kunnert, who begun his NBA career with Buffalo, hit on 14 of 22 shots. Ills previous career high was 29 points and his best this season was 23. 
Tomjanovich and Lucas added 2o points apiece while Malone had 15 points and 13 rebounds. Buffalo rookie 
Adrian Dantley, who missed the 
Braves’ last game with the flu, led all scorers with 33 point*.

Trevino losing that old familiar zip 

1 / 
JL 
• HOW 
MIAMI (A P) •— The old fam iliar swagger is gone. The non-stop chatter has stopped. The broad, expansive gestures are subdued, blurred and indistinct. 
Lee Trevino moves m ore slowly now. 
Ile avoids bending and stooping*wher­ ever possible, often directing his caddy to pick the ball out of the cup. He no longer paces the fairways im patiently between shots, sw inging his arm s, sh ru g g in g h is husky sh o u ld e rs, talking, joking, laughing. 
Now he usually sits quietly on his golf bag, often with his shoulders slumped and his head hanging. 
Oh, there are occasional flashes of the old, fam iliar, on-stage Trevino. 
Waiting to hit his approach shot on the 
72nd hole at Rio P inar last week in the 
Citrus Open, he was pacing back and forth, talking to the gallery, waiting for the group ahead to finish play. • 
“ Lord,” he said to the gallery, “ I wish they’d hurry. I’ve got to go to the bathroom.” 

But that’s unusual these days. And this brash and brassy guy who has added so much to the joy of the gam e has to work at it. 
A gray-faced look of anguished fa­ tigue has replaced the constant, infec­ tious grin. 
He no longer looks at a leaderboard and asks: “ Who do I have to beat?” 
Now the question is, “ Do you think 145 will m ake the cut?" 

‘‘I think he cam e back too soon,” said a close friend and traveling com­ panion. “ I tried to talk him out of it. 
Everybody th at’s close to him tried to talk him out of it. How many tim es have you seen somebody try to come back too soon and then hurt them selves beyond repair? 
“ He just got so antsy at home that he couldn’t stand it— and nobody could stand him. He just had to get back out here.” 
Trevino, whose rags to riches saga now form s an im portant part of the 

 lore and legends of the gam e, is at­ tem pting a return to golf after m ajor back surgery late last year. 
“ The b a c k ’s o k ay ,” he re p lie s, brushing off questions im patiently, almost brusquely. 
But the weariness is evident. T here's obvious pain in his effort to play 18 

 holes. He has nothing left for tne hours and hours of practice that once char­ acterized his gam e. 
“ I have no power in my back, no power in my legs,” he said. “ I just don’t have any power at all anym ore.” 
His problem was illustrated on a par three hole la st w eek. His playing 

 partners hit seven irons to the green. 
Trevino was short with a four iron. 
“ I’ve got to try it for a w hile," he said. “ I’ve got to work at it.” 
He’s playing the next two weeks, then will take at least one week off, maybe more. “ When we start moving north it’s gonna be cold,” he said. 

“ You know how' it can be at Hilton 
Head and Greensboro. And the cold just kills me. Kills me. I can’t move. 
"T hat’s why I wanted to try to come back here in Florida,” he said. “ I’ve always played good here, and the heat is good for me. I thought this would be the best place to try it.”

Kentucky had seen a 14-game win­ ning streak and a 17-game road win­ ning string end at Tennessee Saturday when the Cols won 81-79. 
Givens broke a 12-12 deadlock with just under 12 minutes remaining in the first half by sinking three straight shots to put the Wildcats ahead for good. 
Givens finished with 21 points and 
Robey added 18 as Kentucky lifted its overall mark to 24-3 going into the 
NCAA championship playoffs which begin Saturday. 
The Wildcats built an 11-point half­ time lead against the Bulldogs, reek'd off nine straight points early in the second half to forge in front by 18 points at 45-27, matching their biggest lead of the night which also was equaled just before the buzzer when 
Robey made two free throws. 
Curtis Jackson led Georgia scoring with 14 points and Lavon Mercer added 
12. including a pair of slam-dunks. The defeat left the cellar-dwelling Bulldogs at 3-15 ui the SEC and 9-18 for the year.

Dissension will not hurt 
Cincy says Morgan 

.gets 
JOE MORGAN a kick out of practice 

TAMPA. Fla. (AP) - Joe Morgan, the highest-salaried player in Cincin­ nati history, said Monday that the 
Reds are too protesional to let dissension ruin a bid for a third straight baseball world championship. 
“ Big raises won’t hurt this team. We could have gotten fat last year, but-that didn’t stop us from winning again.” said the 34-year old All-Star second baseman after his first workout of spring training. 
Morgan arrived five days late in camp, with approval from the club, to complete college examinations. 
MVF twice 
Morgan, who became only the se­ cond man to repeat as Most Valuable 
Player in the National League, rejects the notion that 1977 will be a test of compatibility. 
‘‘We will not have problems from within. We will not defeat ourselves,” said Morgan, who recently signed a three-year contract, for a reported $1.2 million. 
The Reds are attempting to become the first National League team ever to win three straight World Series titles. 
The Oakland A’s of 1972-73-74 were the first team in 29 years to achieve the feat, but the franchise has been on the decline since the sweep. 
Remember the A’s 
“ Dissension didn t destroy the /Vs. 
Oakland was torn apart by its owner—not it’s players. Sure, they fought a lot, but they were a team once they were on the field,” Morgan said. 
Even though the team’s winning ways have boosted salaries, Morgan sees no friction developing on the 
Reds. 
“ We have a very special group of guys,” he said. 

Morgan, who hit .329 last year with career highs of 27 home runs and 111 runs batted in, feels the Reds may have slipped in strength by losing ve­ terans Tony Perez and Don Gullet t. 
“ We’re a little weaker, but we're still above everyone else,” he said. 

Morgan said the Los Angeles 
Dodgers improved themselves jvith offseason trades and rank as the Reds chief challenger. 
“ But I still think we ll win our di­ vision by ten games.” Morgan pre­ dicted. 

Johnson gives 
Bruins credit 

NEW YORK (AP) - Marques John­ son says winning the Adolph Rupp 
Trophy is a team effort, just like winning basketball games. 
“ UCLA is not a one-man team and the players on my team helped me look good," Johnson said Monday while picking up the award as The Associat­ ed Press’ College Basketball Player of the Year. “ I'm accepting this award on behalf of my teammates.” 
Johnson, the latest in a long line of great UCLA trontcourt players, ap­ peared at a midtown news conference with his coach. Gene Bartow, and 
Rupp, the winningest coach in college basketball history. 
Modest lad 
While the muscular. 6-foot-7 forward wished to share the wealth with the other UCLA players, Bartow singled out Johnson as the Bruins’ sole driv ing force this season. 
. "It wouldn’t have been a team with­ out him.” said the UCLA coach. “ We had a very young team this year and everyone looked to Marques all year. 
We won the Pac-8 title with him 
Without him. we would have lost it. 
He’s the greatest player in college basketball. He’s the most exciting as well as the most entertaining. Also, he does so much tor us—on the court and oil. He’s a great captain, the ultimate team leader.” 
Bartow also pointed out that national television "didn t hurt his chances for he trophy. In all the games he was on 
TV. he was sensational.” 
Landslide margin 
Johnson took the award in a runaway, outscoring Michigan guard 
Rickey Green 168 votes to 32 i i i the balloting by the nation’s sports writers and broadcasters. Several other players finished far down the line. 
Is he that much better than everyone else? 
“ I just think that if any team would start out with Marques, that team would have a great year,” said Bartow. 

“ Not only is he talented, he’s unsel­ fish. Most times, superstars aren’t that way. But we definitely wouldn’t have been 23-4 without him. He's the anchor of our team ” 
Johnson, a personable, easy talker who is studying communications at the 
I>os Angeles school, acknowledged that the Rupp Trophy enhances his oppor­ tunity for a bigger professional con­ tract. Johnson turned down a chance to go pro last season to finish his senior year at UCLA! 

Top choice 
“ There's going to he some real good money for the first four or five draft picks," noted Johnson, who obviously expects to be among them when the 
National Basketball Association holds its draft this spring. 
Johnson doesn't think he’ll be the top pick. though. 

“ I expect Kent Benson (of Indiana) will go first because some of those teams at the bottom need a dominating center,” Johnson said. 

Rupp, who retired in 1972 after compiling an 879-199 record, presented the trophy to Johnson. The AP Player of the Year receives the Rupp Trophy, which is*awarded by the jconimon- w cal th Athletic Club of Kentucky, a not-for-profit organization dedicated to honoring the former Kentucky coach.

House to halt sports probe

STEREO 

LISTEN TO THE 
.. 
24 Hours 

WASHINGTON (A P) — The House voted Monday not to continue a wide-ranging investigation into professional baseball, basketball, football and hock­ ey- 
By a vote of 271 to 75, the House rejected a resolution tit re-establish a committee that liegun its probe last year. That panel’s authorization ended in 
January. 
Opposition was led by members of the Judiciary 
Committee, who said that panel’s antitrust jurisdic­ tion would be invaded by a probe by another commute** into antitrust implications of pro sports. 
"This resolution would lead to duplication of effort, unnecessary sending and doing unnecessar­ ily the work that another committee has the exper­ tise to do,” said Judiciary Chairman Peter Rodino, 
D-N.J, 
The resolution to re-establish the committee was sponsored by Rep. B F Sisk, D-Calif., the chairman of the old committee. 
Sisk asked that the committee In* reconstituted aud given new powers to look into such areas us sports monopolies, labor relations, player and spectator violence, broadcasting, gambling aud player safety. 
“ We want to look into pro sports us they affect the 
/Xinerican people—lioth the |h*o|>I** directly involved and the fans,” he said 
Tile sports committee would have had the author­ ity to investigate “ all matters relating to proies- sionul sports it deems appropriate” to determine whether legislation is needed 
It would have been directed “ to determine the impact of current antitrust law and policy on professional sports.” 
Professional baseball has long enjoyed an exemp­ tion from antitrust laws. The reconstituted panel also would have been authorized to investigate amateur athletics to the extent they are affected by the problems of pro shirts
